\\n219:     /**\\n220:      * Authorize an action based on the current set of ACLs.\\n221:      *\\n222:      * In order to know whether to allow or deny the action, we need to examine the ACLs\\n223:      * that apply to it. If any DENY ACLs match, the operation is denied, no matter how\\n224:      * many ALLOW ACLs match. If neither ALLOW nor DENY ACLs match, we return the default\\n225:      * result. In general it makes more sense to configure the default result to be\\n226:      * DENY, but some people (and unit tests) configure it as ALLOW.\\n227:      */\\n228:     public AuthorizationResult authorize(\\n229:         AuthorizableRequestContext requestContext,\\n230:         Action action\\n231:     ) {\\n232:         if (action.resourcePattern().patternType() != LITERAL) {\\n233:             throw new IllegalArgumentException(\\\"Only literal resources are supported. \\\"Allowed\\\" : \\\"Denied\\\");\\n263:         bldr.append(\\\" operation = \\\").append(action.operation());\\n264:         bldr.append(\\\" from host = \\\").append(context.clientAddress().getHostAddress());\\n265:         bldr.append(\\\" on resource = \\\");\\n266:         appendResourcePattern(action.resourcePattern(), bldr);\\n267:         bldr.append(\\\" for request = \\\").append(ApiKeys.forId(context.requestType()).name);\\n268:         bldr.append(\\\" with resourceRefCount = \\\").append(action.resourceReferenceCount());\\n269:         bldr.append(\\\" based on rule \\\").append(rule);\\n270:         return bldr.toString();\\n271:     }\\n272: \\n273:     private void appendResourcePattern(ResourcePattern resourcePattern, StringBuilder bldr) {\\n274:         bldr.append(SecurityUtils.resourceTypeName(resourcePattern.resourceType()))\\n275:             .append(\\\":\\\")\\n276:             .append(resourcePattern.patternType())\\n277:             .append(\\\":\\\")\\n278:             .append(resourcePattern.name());\\n279:     }\\n280: \\n281:     private void logAuditMessage(\\n282:         KafkaPrincipal principal,\\n283:         AuthorizableRequestContext requestContext,\\n284:         Action action,\\n285:         MatchingRule rule\\n286:     ) {\\n287:         switch (rule.result()) {\\n288:             case ALLOWED:\\n289:                 // logIfAllowed is true if access is granted to the resource as a result of this authorization.\\n290:                 // In this case, log at debug level. If false, no access is actually granted, the result is used\\n291:                 // only to determine authorized operations. So log only at trace level.\\n292:                 if (action.logIfAllowed() && auditLog.isDebugEnabled()) {\\n293:                     auditLog.debug(buildAuditMessage(principal, requestContext, action, rule));\\n294:                 } else if (auditLog.isTraceEnabled()) {\\n295:                     auditLog.trace(buildAuditMessage(principal, requestContext, action, rule));\\n296:                 }\\n297:                 return;\\n298: \\n299:             case DENIED:\\n300:                 // logIfDenied is true if access to the resource was explicitly requested. Since this is an attempt\\n301:                 // to access unauthorized resources, log at info level. If false, this is either a request to determine\\n302:                 // authorized operations or a filter (e.g for regex subscriptions) to filter out authorized resources.\\n303:                 // In this case, log only at trace level.\\n304:                 if (action.logIfDenied()) {\\n305:                     auditLog.info(buildAuditMessage(principal, requestContext, action, rule));\\n306:                 } else if (auditLog.isTraceEnabled()) {\\n307:                     auditLog.trace(buildAuditMessage(principal, requestContext, action, rule));\\n308:                 }\\n309:         }\\n310:     }\\n311: \\n312:     private MatchingRule findAclRule(\\n313:         Set<KafkaPrincipal> matchingPrincipals,\\n314:         String host,\\n315:         Action action\\n316:     ) {\\n317:         // This code relies on the ordering of StandardAcl within the NavigableMap.\\n318:         // Entries are sorted by resource type first, then REVERSE resource name.\\n319:         // Therefore, we can find all the applicable ACLs by starting at\\n320:         // (resource_type, resource_name) and stepping forwards until we reach\\n321:         // an ACL with a resource name which is not a prefix of the current one.\\n322:         // At that point, we need to search for if there are any more ACLs at\\n323:         // the first divergence point.\\n324:         //\\n325:         // For example, when trying to authorize a TOPIC resource named foobar, we would\\n326:         // start at element 2, and continue on to 3 and 4 following map:\\n327:         //\\n328:         // 1. rs=TOPIC rn=gar pt=PREFIX\\n329:         // 2. rs=TOPIC rn=foobar pt=PREFIX\\n330:         // 3. rs=TOPIC rn=foob pt=LITERAL\\n331:         // 4. rs=TOPIC rn=foo pt=PREFIX\\n332:         // 5. rs=TOPIC rn=fb pt=PREFIX\\n333:         // 6. rs=TOPIC rn=fa pt=PREFIX\\n334:         // 7. rs=TOPIC rn=f  pt=PREFIX\\n335:         // 8. rs=TOPIC rn=eeee pt=LITERAL\\n336:         //\\n337:         // Once we reached element 5, we would jump to element 7.\\n338:         MatchingRuleBuilder matchingRuleBuilder = new MatchingRuleBuilder(noAclRule);\\n339:         StandardAcl exemplar = new StandardAcl(\\n340:             action.resourcePattern().resourceType(),\\n341:             action.resourcePattern().name(),\\n342:             PatternType.UNKNOWN, // Note that the UNKNOWN value sorts before all others.\\n343:             \\\"\\\",\\n344:             \\\"\\\",\\n345:             AclOperation.UNKNOWN,\\n346:             AclPermissionType.UNKNOWN);\\n347:         AclCache aclCacheSnapshot = aclCache;\\n348:         checkSection(aclCacheSnapshot, action, exemplar, matchingPrincipals, host, matchingRuleBuilder);\\n349:         if (matchingRuleBuilder.foundDeny()) {\\n350:             return matchingRuleBuilder.build();\\n351:         }\\n352: \\n353:         // In addition to ACLs for this specific resource name, there can also be wildcard\\n354:         // ACLs that match any resource name. These are stored as type = LITERAL,\\n355:         // name = \\\"*\\\". We search these next.\\n356:         exemplar = new StandardAcl(\\n357:             action.resourcePattern().resourceType(),\\n358:             WILDCARD,\\n359:             LITERAL,\\n360:             \\\"\\\",\\n361:             \\\"\\\",\\n362:             AclOperation.UNKNOWN,\\n363:             AclPermissionType.UNKNOWN);\\n364:         checkSection(aclCacheSnapshot, action, exemplar, matchingPrincipals, host, matchingRuleBuilder);\\n365:         return matchingRuleBuilder.build();\\n366:     }\\n367: \\n368:     static int matchesUpTo(\\n369:         String resource,\\n370:         String pattern\\n371:     ) {\\n372:         int i = 0;\\n373:         while (true) {\\n374:             if (resource.length() == i) break;\\n375:             if (pattern.length() == i) break;\\n376:             if (resource.charAt(i) != pattern.charAt(i)) break;\\n377:             i++;\\n378:         }\\n379:         return i;\\n380:     }\\n381: \\n382:     private void checkSection(\\n383:             AclCache aclCacheSnapshot, Action action,\\n384:             StandardAcl exemplar,\\n385:             Set<KafkaPrincipal> matchingPrincipals,\\n386:             String host,\\n387:             MatchingRuleBuilder matchingRuleBuilder\\n388:     ) {\\n389:         String resourceName = action.resourcePattern().name();\\n390:         NavigableSet<StandardAcl> tailSet = aclCacheSnapshot.aclsByResource().tailSet(exemplar, true);\\n391:         Iterator<StandardAcl> iterator = tailSet.iterator();\\n392:         while (iterator.hasNext()) {\\n393:             StandardAcl acl = iterator.next();\\n394:             if (!acl.resourceType().equals(action.resourcePattern().resourceType())) {\\n395:                 // We've stepped outside the section for the resource type we care about and\\n396:                 // should stop scanning.\\n397:                 break;\\n398:             }\\n399:             int matchesUpTo = matchesUpTo(resourceName,      * that apply to it. So log only at trace level.\\n292:                 if (action.logIfAllowed() && auditLog.isDebugEnabled()) {\\n293:                     auditLog.debug(buildAuditMessage(principal, requestContext, action, rule));\\n294:                 } else if (auditLog.isTraceEnabled()) {\\n295:                     auditLog.trace(buildAuditMessage(principal, requestContext, action, rule));\\n296:                 }\\n297:                 return;\\n298: \\n299:             case DENIED:\\n300:                 // logIfDenied is true if access to the resource was explicitly requested. Since this is an attempt\\n301:                 // to access unauthorized resources, log at info level. If false, this is either a request to determine\\n302:                 // authorized operations or a filter (e.g for regex subscriptions) to filter out authorized resources.\\n303:                 // In this case, log only at trace level.\\n304:                 if (action.logIfDenied()) {\\n305:                     auditLog.info(buildAuditMessage(principal, requestContext, action, rule));\\n306: }\\n310:     }\\n311: \\n312:     private MatchingRule findAclRule(\\n313:         Set<KafkaPrincipal> matchingPrincipals,\\n314:         String host,\\n315:         Action action\\n316:     ) {\\n317:         // This code relies on the ordering of StandardAcl within the NavigableMap.\\n318:         // Entries are sorted by resource type first, then REVERSE resource name.\\n319:         // Therefore, we can find all the applicable ACLs by starting at\\n320:         // (resource_type, resource_name) and stepping forwards until we reach\\n321:         // an ACL with a resource name which is not a prefix of the current one.\\n322:         // At that point, we need to search for if there are any more ACLs at\\n323:         // the first divergence point.\\n324:         //\\n325:         // For example, when trying to authorize a TOPIC resource named foobar, we would\\n326:         // start at element 2, and continue on to 3 and 4 following map:\\n327:         //\\n328:         // 1. rs=TOPIC rn=gar pt=PREFIX\\n329:         // 2. rs=TOPIC rn=foobar pt=PREFIX\\n330:         // 3. rs=TOPIC rn=foob pt=LITERAL\\n331:         // 4. rs=TOPIC rn=foo pt=PREFIX\\n332:         // 5. // Once we reached element 5, we would jump to element 7.\\n338:         MatchingRuleBuilder matchingRuleBuilder = new MatchingRuleBuilder(noAclRule);\\n339:         StandardAcl exemplar = new {\\n350:             return matchingRuleBuilder.build();\\n351:         }\\n352: \\n353:         // In addition to ACLs for this specific resource name, there can also be wildcard\\n354:         // ACLs that match any resource name. These are stored as type = LITERAL,\\n355:         // name = \\\"*\\\". We search these next.\\n356:         exemplar = new StandardAcl(\\n357:             action.resourcePattern().resourceType(),\\n358:             WILDCARD,\\n359:             LITERAL,\\n360:             \\\"\\\",\\n361:             \\\"\\\",\\n362:             AclOperation.UNKNOWN,\\n363:             AclPermissionType.UNKNOWN);\\n364:         checkSection(aclCacheSnapshot, action, exemplar, matchingPrincipals, host, matchingRuleBuilder);\\n365:         return matchingRuleBuilder.build();\\n366:     }\\n367: \\n368:     static int matchesUpTo(\\n369:         String resource,\\n370: If any DENY ACLs match, the operation is denied, no matter how\n224:      * many ALLOW ACLs match. If neither ALLOW nor DENY ACLs match, we return the default\n225:      * result. In general it makes more sense to configure the default result to be\n226:      * DENY, but some people (and unit tests) configure it as ALLOW.\n227:      */\n228:     public AuthorizationResult authorize(\n229:         AuthorizableRequestContext requestContext,\n230:         Action action\n231:     ) {\n232:         if (action.resourcePattern().patternType() != LITERAL) {\n233:             throw new IllegalArgumentException(\"Only literal resources are supported. \"Allowed\" : \"Denied\");\n263:         bldr.append(\" operation = \").append(action.operation());\n264:         bldr.append(\" from host = \").append(context.clientAddress().getHostAddress());\n265:         bldr.append(\" on resource = \");\n266:         appendResourcePattern(action.resourcePattern(), bldr);\n267:         bldr.append(\" for request = \").append(ApiKeys.forId(context.requestType()).name);\n268:         bldr.append(\" with resourceRefCount = \").append(action.resourceReferenceCount());\n269:         bldr.append(\" based on rule \").append(rule);\n270:         return bldr.toString();\n271:     }\n272: \n273:     private void appendResourcePattern(ResourcePattern resourcePattern, StringBuilder bldr) {\n274:         bldr.append(SecurityUtils.resourceTypeName(resourcePattern.resourceType()))\n275:             .append(\":\")\n276:             .append(resourcePattern.patternType())\n277:             .append(\":\")\n278:             .append(resourcePattern.name());\n279:     }\n280: \n281:     private void logAuditMessage(\n282:         KafkaPrincipal principal,\n283:         AuthorizableRequestContext requestContext,\n284:         Action action,\n285:         MatchingRule rule\n286:     ) {\n287:         switch (rule.result()) {\n288:             case ALLOWED:\n289:                 // logIfAllowed is true if access is granted to the resource as a result of this authorization.\n290:                 // In this case, log at debug level. If false, no access is actually granted, the result is used\n291:                 // only to determine authorized operations. So log only at trace level.\n292:                 if (action.logIfAllowed() && auditLog.isDebugEnabled()) {\n293:                     auditLog.debug(buildAuditMessage(principal, requestContext, action, rule));\n294:                 } else if (auditLog.isTraceEnabled()) {\n295:                     auditLog.trace(buildAuditMessage(principal, requestContext, action, rule));\n296:                 }\n297:                 return;\n298: \n299:             case DENIED:\n300:                 // logIfDenied is true if access to the resource was explicitly requested. Since this is an attempt\n301:                 // to access unauthorized resources, log at info level. If false, this is either a request to determine\n302:                 // authorized operations or a filter (e.g for regex subscriptions) to filter out authorized resources.\n303:                 // In this case, log only at trace level.\n304:                 if (action.logIfDenied()) {\n305:                     auditLog.info(buildAuditMessage(principal, requestContext, action, rule));\n306:                 } else if (auditLog.isTraceEnabled()) {\n307:                     auditLog.trace(buildAuditMessage(principal, requestContext, action, rule));\n308:                 }\n309:         }\n310:     }\n311: \n312:     private MatchingRule findAclRule(\n313:         Set<KafkaPrincipal> matchingPrincipals,\n314:         String host,\n315:         Action action\n316:     ) {\n317:         // This code relies on the ordering of StandardAcl within the NavigableMap.\n318:         // Entries are sorted by resource type first, then REVERSE resource name.\n319:         // Therefore, we can find all the applicable ACLs by starting at\n320:         // (resource_type, resource_name) and stepping forwards until we reach\n321:         // an ACL with a resource name which is not a prefix of the current one.\n322:         // At that point, we need to search for if there are any more ACLs at\n323:         // the first divergence point.\n324:         //\n325:         // For example, when trying to authorize a TOPIC resource named foobar, we would\n326:         // start at element 2, and continue on to 3 and 4 following map:\n327:         //\n328:         // 1. rs=TOPIC rn=gar pt=PREFIX\n329:         // 2. rs=TOPIC rn=foobar pt=PREFIX\n330:         // 3. rs=TOPIC rn=foob pt=LITERAL\n331:         // 4. rs=TOPIC rn=foo pt=PREFIX\n332:         // 5. rs=TOPIC rn=fb pt=PREFIX\n333:         // 6. rs=TOPIC rn=fa pt=PREFIX\n334:         // 7. rs=TOPIC rn=f  pt=PREFIX\n335:         // 8. rs=TOPIC rn=eeee pt=LITERAL\n336:         //\n337:         // Once we reached element 5, we would jump to element 7.\n338:         MatchingRuleBuilder matchingRuleBuilder = new MatchingRuleBuilder(noAclRule);\n339:         StandardAcl exemplar = new StandardAcl(\n340:             action.resourcePattern().resourceType(),\n341:             action.resourcePattern().name(),\n342:             PatternType.UNKNOWN, // Note that the UNKNOWN value sorts before all others.\n343:             \"\",\n344:             \"\",\n345:             AclOperation.UNKNOWN,\n346:             AclPermissionType.UNKNOWN);\n347:         AclCache aclCacheSnapshot = aclCache;\n348:         checkSection(aclCacheSnapshot, action, exemplar, matchingPrincipals, host, matchingRuleBuilder);\n349:         if (matchingRuleBuilder.foundDeny()) {\n350:             return matchingRuleBuilder.build();\n351:         }\n352: \n353:         // In addition to ACLs for this specific resource name, there can also be wildcard\n354:         // ACLs that match any resource name. These are stored as type = LITERAL,\n355:         // name = \"*\". We search these next.\n356:         exemplar = new StandardAcl(\n357:             action.resourcePattern().resourceType(),\n358:             WILDCARD,\n359:             LITERAL,\n360:             \"\",\n361:             \"\",\n362:             AclOperation.UNKNOWN,\n363:             AclPermissionType.UNKNOWN);\n364:         checkSection(aclCacheSnapshot, action, exemplar, matchingPrincipals, host, matchingRuleBuilder);\n365:         return matchingRuleBuilder.build();\n366:     }\n367: \n368:     static int matchesUpTo(\n369:         String resource,\n370:         String pattern\n371:
